When the tears of the eyes descend from the veins that are on top of the head due to heat, and medical treatment does not help, and you see the face of the patient turn red, and feel on the forehead movement as if trembling; and the eyes are thin and moist so that the hair of the eyelids fall out, and the eyelids are heated and scorched by the ardor of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it «treatment for contusion», and that is what you do at the back of the patient who has this disease, let him have the hairs on his forehead, then make III cuts on his forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and one of the cuts should be as II fingers right in the middle of the forehead going down to the nose, and the other II on both sides above the temples, and beware of the arteries that are on both sides above the temples; and keep your hand away from the connection of the two jaws, and each wound should be the quantity of III fingers across; and prepare a piece of sponge and much cloth for wiping the blood, then pour the strong spatumile made of II parts as is its form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the cut which is next to the temple up to the second cut; and peel all the skin that is between the two cuts to the surface which is on top of the bone, then do likewise from the middle cut to the other second one, and then apply this strong spatumile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	so place in the first cut the instrument which is called "cultellaire", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is smooth, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp side towards the diseased flesh of the heart, and the smooth side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous until it reaches what opens into the heart, and then make another in the middle cut until the other side; and then drain the blood evenly, and press the area for the drained blood; then place a wick of old cotton in each cut, and put on cloths moistened with wine and oil and egg white, and guard against hot abscesses forming; and on the third day loosen the bandage, and apply plenty of warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments used to cure wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the realm of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When to anyone comes a sharp and usual catarrh, and you see the eyes dim and small, and weakening the sight, and the eyelids burned; and the hair falls out, and on the head there comes an acute pain, and the patient sneezes; then know by these accidents that those matters and this catarrh do not come from anywhere but many veins, and the most effective cure that there is, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to lie down with his head backward, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another on the wide temple.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go as far as the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves in the temples that move during eating; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two edges of the incision and put old cotton and flaxen threads; then bind on top cloths moistened in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses; when they are removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying agents that promote fleshing over.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flower, and four parts of colofonium, and make a plaster; and administer it on these wounds to quicken flesh growth.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the deafness of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains, or insects, or small stones or similar things such as iron; or seeds, such as beans, peas, lentils; or flowing substances such as water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or any other kind of thing that does not fit in the ear and does not grow in the ear falls into it, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, distill a small amount of violet oil or flaxseed oil, then proceed with extraction; and make him sneeze with condice, and plug his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and stretch the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times pus comes out by this treatment; and if it does not come out, proceed with extraction using fine tweezers, of which the form is here described:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the tweezers, that is good; if not, proceed with extraction using a fine needle of small gauge; and if it does not come out by this means, make a cane of iron and place the tip of the cane in the opening of the ear firmly, and plug what is around the cane with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the cane; then pull forcefully, as pus often comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in such manner, take glue from which birds take, and place some instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not heal from all the things that we have said, then you must hurry to split the ear so as to prevent a hot abscess and spasm; and the method of splitting is such that you first let blood from the patient’s cephalic vein according to the measure of their strength, then sit the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fat where it hangs; and let the cut be like a crescent until you reach the bone, then remove it as much as you can, and suck quickly with your mouth; and treat until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and they swell, then administer an extraction; and if it cannot come out, then apply the spatula gently according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and to administer an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grains are moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract them with subtle tweezers and a suction device, as we have said, so that the extraction is light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of fluid that falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use sneezing first, and stuff the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on that same ear where the fluid is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out through that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, then take many stones according to the length of your thumb, thin and light, and heat them somewhat in the fire; and have the patient place one or more into the opening of his ear, and jump up with one foot from another side, and strike with another stone upon the stone which is in the ear; and do not cease doing this from stone to stone until all the water comes out entirely, and thus it will come out completely; and if you wish, take some reeds, and put one end into the ear, and heat the other end with fire until the thinnest part of the reed is burned; then do again with other reeds until all the water comes out as we have said with the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the creature, if it is small in body, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large in body that one can feel it, then use the extraction with tweezers; and it is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of yellow worms from the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the section and in the treatment of distillations, and if the treatment does not help, then you must look at the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, then pull them out with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, then take the cane from which is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the finest end into the ear according to the extent of the patient's suffering, then suck hard on the entire cane; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, wrap cotton around the cane as I have said for the stone; and if they do not come out forcefully as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have tested for worm occlusion, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, whose form is as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether of silver or brass, narrow below at small openings and above for dripping; and to press inside the distillation with a well-made brass instrument for that purpose, and if you want use the dropper and wrap around the point properly with cotton; then throw your oil or juice in, and what you want of your medicines into the tube, and the tube should be in the ear; then pour into the dropper all the cotton, and press your hand moderately so that the oil is distilled into the ear canal; and the patient feels it inside, and let the distillation pot be heated a bit over fire before you distill into the ear; and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the obstruction of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	Some children are born who have no openings in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to blockage from a wound, or of matter born within the ear, and these blockages sometimes occur deep inside the ear, so one cannot see them; and sometimes it happens that the point blocks the opening, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes deep inside, so one cannot see it, is of difficult healing in many conditions, and for the one that can be seen you must put the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the obstruction clearly, then apply all this spatumile, of which here is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be smooth and sharp on both sides entirely, so that it does not hurt the ear; if the obstruction is of matter born or flesh from inside the ear, then hold it with fine tweezers, and cut lightly until all the matter is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstruction is completely in the ear, then take a fine light scraper and warm it slightly over fire, then place it in the core of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the obstruction from which the patient feels difficulty in hearing, pierce lightly, and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a plug according to the width of the opening, and anoint it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or take a plug and anoint it with rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on it; and if you see the ear swollen, then you must remove the plug and replace it with another plug anointed with cerate made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then clean it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge and cloths in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papermakers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This ailment that comes from papermakers' eyes when they are moist and then dry, you should stretch them with tweezers and brushes, and cut them out with a spatula from their roots; then put ground vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they do not heal from this, then cauterize them with a fine lenticular cautery and the cautery after the incision is very useful; and they often recur because something remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, things that resemble hail in their form and hardness come upon the eyelids, and for this reason, this disease is called "hail," and it is a collection of moisture thick on the skin above and below; the treatment is such: take notice if the hail moves from one side to another, and it is easy to know; then cut it open widely, then gently peel each part, then take it with tweezers, and remove it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you cannot cut it without piercing a bit the skin, then do not worry about the patient; and if the incision is large, then sew it up, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, then do nothing forcefully, for the ointments will restore it soon and promote flesh growth.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the wax is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then invert the paper, and extend the wax with tweezers, and cut and press from both sides; and if the paper is moved away by the incision, it does not matter; and when the wax is cut, wash the eye with salt water, and clean the place of that which clogs until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that clogs the upper part of the eye membranes, and this happens more to children than to other people, and it greatly troubles their eyes, causing them to have catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sun's light because tears rush to their eyes; therefore, they lie on their faces immediately and sleep thus, and their eyelashes under their eyebrows are moist as the swelling and appearance are covered with exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the extraneous matter between.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the work is that the patient puts his head in your lap; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains extraneous matter from each part, then place it on him; and press with your hands from one side and the other so that the extraneous matter be gathered within the circle; then cut in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a slit as wide, and let it not be larger than the wound you make at the vein incision; and cut the skin thoroughly until you reach the extraneous matter; and in many dispositions comes extraneous matter from the slit, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract it then with a piece of cloth wrapped between your fingers against the wind, and turn your hand to right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to insert it into the crack, that you do not come all the way to the pupil, that you do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the extraneous matter does not open at the beginning of the crack, then slightly enlarge the crack until it opens; then extract it as we have said, then wet cloths in oil and water, and place them on the area, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are such people who grind ash and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the place hot, then treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	the hairs of the eyelids
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs other than those natural grow in the eyelids and are irritated, they harm the eyes and cause various ailments such as habitual tears and softening of the eyelids and leukoma, to the point that it is a cause for the destruction of the eyes; and the treatment follows four methods: by cautery with fire together, or by medicine according to what was said before in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by cantharides, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the head of the patient in your hand, then turn the eyelid towards your left hand; if it turns, that is good; if not, insert a needle with thread over it; and do this near the edge where the hair grows next to these hairs, pull the thread across all the eyelid, and turn it to the razor; then cut in the part below the eyelid, below the fixed hairs, along the entire speculum from the large tear duct to the small one; then extract the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and cloth under the eyelid, then apply on top of the eyelid a figure like an interlace, as the leaf of myrtle, and always it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you wish to lift the eyelid which is divided into all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And thus there are some who need to cut a large quantity of the eyelid according to how soft the eyelid is; then make an incision all over the spatule on the two lines that you have marked, and start from the large larmier down to the small; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the lancet into one of the two angles of the area, then peel it entirely; then join the two edges with a stitch of a needle with an entire thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and remove the excess threads on both eyelids with some sticky substances if you wish to do so; and if not, then don’t care about it, then leave the stitch and the threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitches using drying and binding things, because the eyelid rises at the healing of the wound and its joining together, but the stitch is more harmful (as the ancients said), and this work is without fear; and there is another method: which is to mark the eyelid with a shape that is as if it were a myrtle leaf, just like we have described, three inches apart according to the form that is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut what protrudes above the small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the tweezers, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with thread, and insert it into the figure; and place one thread beside the large eyelid, and the other thread beside the small, and bring together between your fingers the threads equally; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin where you have marked, as we have recounted, then bring together the two lips of the wound by stitching, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes happens that the hairs of the eyelid are turned inward: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more intricate.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the canes is according to this form: you must turn the parchment and cut inside as I have said, then make two canes by art, and two subtle threads as long as the parchment and as wide as the spatula is; then cut at both ends where you hold the threads; then join one and the other subtly on that which rises above the parchment of the eye, and extract the two canes from both parts properly; leave it thus for some days, and the skin which was constrained will die, dry up, and shed, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cut it with force, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is sealed, and the parchment is lifted, the hairs will no longer grow; and this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle and put the silk thread through it, thin and fine; then bring together the shoulders and tie one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then arrange in the container another fine silk thread briefly, and tie the head of the thread; then have the patient's head in your hand; and let it be near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is delicate and minute work; then push the needle to the root of the hair attached all through the container, and make it pierce into the paper quickly until you pull it over the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the container, and put in the container that hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out of the container onto the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the shaft is treated and the hair does not come out with it, you will pull the shaft from below along all the thread that you have arranged there, until the shaft comes out of the hole above and you see it with your eye; then you will pull the shaft and the thread, close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair burns in its place and flesh grows over; and if the hair is small, add one long hair from natural hair, and raise it along with that which you leave there, until it is raised and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the pus from the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the pus comes to the eye, there are two ways it can occur: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by the suddenness of a wound, or of a cutting, or of a cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of the work in it is that you split that suture, separate its lips, and put linen tents inside, and leave it until it is healed; and it does not befit you to use in its treatment things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease returns worse than before; but use softening things, such as fenugreek; and the decoction of water or ale and flaxseed should be cooked, and ointments of aquilon melted in any of the oils, and wrap a tent around it, and cure it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your care is that you take heed that it does not heal according to the form it was before; and this work which we have spoken of is nothing but remedies for this disease so that it does not return in the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is beneath is truly called "axacrati," and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of working with it is that you take a needle, in which there is double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left eyelid to the right so that the thread comes out two fingers away from the flesh; then stretch the flesh above all the needle, and cut it one span wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the membrane returns according to what is appropriate, it’s good; if not, take a scraper and put it in the split, and turn the membrane, and make two cuts on the inside of the membrane; and let the ends of the two cuts be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make one angle so that when they are joined together, the shape is like the shape of a letter called «I griesche»; then remove that flesh according to the amount its sides are sharp below, from what surrounds the membrane, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then cure it with what we have said about softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a split or a suture or a cautery, then you must make a full cut below the hairs of the membranes, as mentioned above; then separate between the two edges of a bandage, as I have said; and the work should be done according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters devise ingeniously with all their power how they might return the shape to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is needed for the work and instruments in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the suddenness of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this welding happens to men in such a way that the paper above is soldered with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural works, then you must put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and stretch it with pincers, until you cut off what is hard with a subtle spatula, which is not too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient cannot bear if the sharp spatula wounds the eye; and let your incision, with which you peel off that assembly, be lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and heal all of that assembly, and sometimes make salty water in the eye, and lift it up with sweet water, and with collyrium; then place between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and put on the eye wool soaked in egg white; and after the third day use the collyrium and things to solder until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: one is nervous and similar to a hard surface, and another which is not nervous, but resembles white moisture frozen, which when one touches it with iron and tries to pare it with tweezers, one cannot; and both appearances begin near the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover all the sight and all the light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of the incision is that the patient places his head in your hand, then you work the eyes; and lift the paper in your hand, then cut the nail with tweezers of small padding, and extend it above; then take a needle, and put horsehair or ox hair or cow hair, and strong thread; and double the tip of the needle a little and insert it into the nail, and pierce through all the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it above, and peel off all the hair on the side of the nail next to the pupil and sew the hair up to the top, then cut the remainder at the root of the tear duct using all the spatula finely and with small force, and leave the natural flesh or tear duct so that the usual flow of tears does not come through the incision; sometimes extend the nail only by an inch and with thread, as we have said; then peel it off completely with a fine spatula as described here is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take care that the spatula does not touch the flesh membrane and break it, and that the pupil is not pierced; and after the incision throw into the eye a bit of pounded silkworm excrement, and of collyrium made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then clean it with what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not fleshy, and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this kind of nail resemblance is often treated with medicines; and they grow as I have described in the section, and if you want to cut it, you work on the patient's eye using the spatula slightly sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail gently from above, and if you see that it does not thin out and the inflammation presses in, then distill into the eye with your mouth a collyrium made of litharge and red collyrium and pounded silkworm excrement, and plug the eye until the next day; then begin the work again according to this same method, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If anything is not contrary in the eye, such as a warm abscess, then leave it and first treat the warm abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the eyelid harms the eye by great damage, then suspend it with a needle, and cut off part of it but not all, so that tears do not come; then instill in the eye red collyrium which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In the eyes of some men, red flesh sometimes grows and covers the pupil, pressing on the papillae and turning them inward, resembling a pomegranate blossom; and the work is such that the patient places his head in your hand, then you operate on the eyes, and cut all that flesh with suitable needles for this purpose, holding it firmly; then cut off the first layer of flesh, going all the way to the scraper until the end, taking care not to injure the eye during the work; and let the incision be from the spatula we have mentioned in the incision of the nail and the small forces with which you remove the seal, as is shown after this chapter; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh removed, then apply the oil of burnt glass or instill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines, and place a cotton cover on the eye tied with egg white, so that it does not become inflamed; and if anything remains and warm blood flows, and you fear an abscess may occur, leave the eye alone and treat the inflammation with soothing remedies for hot abscesses; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do when flesh is attached in the eye by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless you must lighten the treatment of each weak eye by the natural way; and by the accidental way, in iron work; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this limb can bear this work.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Bloodshot veins that cover the eye, and hinder the sight's work and weaken the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is then necessary first to examine if the eye in which the bloodshot occurs is strong and has no other disease besides the bloodshot; then proceed in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head on your lap, then suspend those veins for a whole ounce according to your wisdom, and let the ounces be doubled as per this method:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two oncinies by degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then when you coil those subtle veins with force, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see those veins move out of the eye; and be careful not to injure the eye with the points of the spatula, and do this work at midday in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut outside of those veins; and when you have done this, distill into the eye green and red collyria to corrupt what remains of the sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all of this in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of things that ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and you are sure of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this method that is before until it is healed; and this is the form of the force:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The doctors call it "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and hot medicinal fire as I have said before, and it is not healed, then it is necessary that you cut into the abscess where it should be opened, and draw out all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then scrape it all with this instrument which has the following form; and it is called "aspre chief," and it should be made of iron with a sharp end, and pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the corrupted part of the bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is scraped off; and do this several times, then restore the area with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the sinus is sealed and flesh grows there, and the body of the vein is sealed, and remains this way for forty days, and it does not renew or become abscessed, and no adverse incident occurs, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other method but to return the fistula to the opening of the sinus in this manner: which is to uncover the bone a second time by iron and with medicinal cauterization, and when it is uncovered you take a forceps in this form, and let the head of the iron be three-angled, and the shaft be tapered up to the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and keep your hand a little away from the eye, then turn the forceps completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it by the wind that comes out if he holds his hand over his sinus; and afterwards restore the area with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens in the place, the matter goes to the sinus; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the discharge from the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is fully and entirely open, and there comes no obstruction to the nerve, nor diminishment, then you should bind the patient; then heal it, then apply leeches or a suction cup without pricking to draw out, then put on the eye a bandage made of acacia and aloes and frankincense and storax, and then strain the eye, and cover it with plasters and cloths; and the method of the cloths is that you take cloths quite soft, and double each one four times, and then place one over another according to the amount the eye needs; then tightly bind above with a strong bandage, and repeat the suction cups without pricking; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the bandages soften, then you must strain it very much; then remove the binding after the day and night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not; then restart the plasters and cloths and the binding and the suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the breaking of woven tissue
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the woven tissue, it then opens up, and fibers come out like resin grains, which is astonishing to see; then if you see it cut, the work is such that you push a needle into the root of the part below all the way to the top part, then insert another needle where there is double thread from the tear edge; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the tissue around, and bind it well, then remove the needle and put on the eye moistened wool in an egg white; and leave it until the threads fall with the tissue, then treat the eye with things that comfort until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the tissue on both sides of a circle of cloth until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows great appearance, then pierce it with a subtle spatula that comes from the perfection of the eye, and draw the white moisture down and into the eye, and enter thus quickly; then extract until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the white of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing more than white that gathers in the eye, resembling descending water, but it is not water; and the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take his head between your two hands, and move it until you see the white come up to your eyes; then let it stay fixed, and do not let it descend and break the light, so that the patient can see things as usual; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the white is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	seat the patient between your hands, then take the thin spatula and cut into the corneal layer with the continuation of the conjunctive with the cornea and the crown, until the pus comes out; and when it has come out, distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek has been boiled and honey, then cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the similarities of the waters in the division, and what is needed for piercing; then work according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you seat the patient between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and bind his healthy eye tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand if the eye is right; then put the tip of the instrument near the cornea by the thickness of a hair at that gland of the eye to the part of the lesser lachrymator, then thrust the instrument called "almagda" forcefully, and turn your hand until it pierces into the gland of the eye, and feel when almagda comes to the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the way of almagda be exactly the same as the measurement from the pupil to the end of the iris; and this is the cornea of the eye; you will see the bone through the paper because of the clarity of the corneal layer, and then place the instrument until it reaches where the water is, then squeeze it under one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the aqueous humor is now dislodged, the patient sees it in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest for a little while, if the aqueous humor rises through the second channel, apply force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and does not rise, then extract the almagda gently by turning your hand little by little; and then put in a bit of clear gem essence, and lift the eye from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply to the eye pledgets or wool soaked in rose oil and egg white, and bind with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply ground cumin mixed with egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument which is called "alberit", of which here is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce then the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make the place subtle, then put in almagda, as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a comfortable sleep, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and let him be free from all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his condition until the third day; then release him in that same dark room, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then rebind him until the seventh day; and it is not appropriate for you to do this at the time of the treatment or after the incision now, but it is necessary for you to lighten this, because the liquid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When abscesses come with heat, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and address it with what soothes abscess; and when it is calmed, then unbind the vision and place on his face an eyeshade to cover for some days, and be now in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then gradually leave the house little by little, and return to his usual activities; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Yemen, who told us that in his country they make pierced almagda, which one sucks the water out of, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, for those who do not understand them see them; and they are of proper brass:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the front end of this same fineness be and the back end in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes flesh is born on the nose in various forms, some of which resemble scorpions with many legs; and there are those where the flesh is engraved in a fox-colored hue, and also has smooth flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these smooth flesh, which is not engraved, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; then work his nostrils, apply the ointment to that flesh, and pull it hard; then cut what you can sustain with a fine sharp spatula on one side until you know that all the flesh has been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains something that one cannot cut, then open it all with subtle and light instruments so that nothing remains; and if the pus is abundant or the abscess hot, aid it as necessary; and if they are malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize until the pus is exhausted and all the matter removed, then apply a cool and moist dressing with water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose bleeds and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healing; and if moisture does not emerge properly, know that there is dead matter in the bone above which the instruments cannot reach to cut: then you must insert a linen thread somewhat thick, and tie it by knots of about an inch or less apart; and have the patient put the end of the thread into his nostril as far as possible, and pull on it gently until it comes through inside the mouth; and many times children in schools do this, and it is easy for one who wants to do it; then hold the end that comes out of the nostril with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and untie the knots one after another as they are drawn through.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the gnats have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe the blood, and soak the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode everything remaining of the flesh; and then place a linen plug in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, into which one distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and guide it thus; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be filled to purify the head; and have a handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.
