et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of the work is that you instruct the patient to keep the intestines inside with his hand in the wound if he can enter it; then place pressure on his neck between your hands, and lift the legs; then stretch the abdomen upwards, and cut all the skin from the scrotum lengthwise; then insert hooks into the lower part of the waist according to what you need to open the wound, and they should be such that the pus can come out; then peel off the surface beneath the scrotal skin until the hard white surface is completely exposed; then put your index finger in what follows the testicle, between the white surface under the egg skin and the second layer of skin, and separate what is behind the egg and between the second layer of skin; and move with your right hand inside the abdomen of the scrotum, and lift the hard white surface upwards with your left hand, and raise the egg towards the waist; then command the assistant to stretch the egg upwards and untie what is around behind the bandage; feel with your fingers if there is any intestine wrapped in the hard white surface, and if you find anything, place it inside the abdomen beneath; then take a needle with thick thread made of ten threads, and insert it into the back part of the skin, which is after the scrotal skin; below the waist, cut off the visible ends of the threads so that there are four threads left; then arrange them one on top of another in the shape of a cross, and tie the skin tightly with two strong knots as we have said it is beneath the scrotal skin; wrap the threads around the stitches firmly with two knots so that none of the vessels that nourish cannot enter inside, so no hot abscess can form; then place another knot according to the first long stitch by two fingers length, and after these two knots leave a large space of one finger from the surface beneath the scrotum's skin; then follow all around according to the roundness that the egg bears; then cut in the part below the scrotal skin until it is smooth, and apply ointment as we have said earlier; then administer moistened woolen cloth with oil, place it on the wounds, and apply the bandage as we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white surface that we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, due to fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and let the ligament be until it falls off by itself; and if it delays in falling, it should be soaked with hot water, and apply what we have said, until it falls; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshly hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone who would dare to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the branch which is together with the vine, in such a manner that you bind the vessels after cutting slightly underneath; then cut in the middle, and treat the abscess of what is worked on until the vessels fall out; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes rupture occurs in the bowels, as we have said, and the area opens up; and none of the intestines should hang down to the groin, and if they do hang down, it is bad, and repairs happen continuously; and still, if it stays too long at this point, the wound grows or the sphacelus enlarges until the intestines hang down; and this happens due to the stretching of the sphacelus which is in the bowels, as we have said, for it stretches out, then softens and swells up the area and opens up; and the treatment is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this way: and that is when the patient lies down on their back between your hands, then cut the swollen part of the rupture according to a length of three fingers; and then remove the sphacelus which is under the skin that follows, then take the rod and put it over the visible area of the sphacelus; and press it perfectly against the abdomen, then sew up the two visible areas of the sphacelus at the top of the rod, sewing one and the other; then remove the top of the rod, and do not cut any part of the sphacelus nor stretch the eye or anything else, as I have made known to you in the treatment for the prolapse of the intestines; then treat it with the treatment for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the fibers, then dress and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The suture is tight, and there is no appearance in the rupture, and the cauterization is lighter in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of the testicles becomes softened in some men because the flesh inside is softened, and it is clear to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to treat it, that the patient lies on his back, and cut the softened skin over the natural skin; then bring together the two lips with a suture, and if you wish, sew first the excess of the softened skin with three or four firm sutures; then cut between the sutures, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	from the chaste one
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that chastisements are scorned in our law, and for this reason it would please me not to speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary except for two reasons: the first is that doctors should know how to respond when asked, and know the treatment; and the second is because we often need the chaste ones of some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castrations are done in two ways: either by attraction, or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we do by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and hanging; then take them in your hand, until they retract and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For the castration of the animal: you must paint the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie up the suspensory ligament, and cut on each egg once, when you have properly skinned them; and leave some of the surface and the fine surface that is on the vessels; and this method of castration is milder than that which is done by traction, because in traction something of the testicles may remain by chance, by which the beast desires lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	about hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism occurs in two ways in humans: one is when between the two testicles there appears something like the structure of a woman's genitalia, where there may be hair, and sometimes it also expels urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another manner is in women, and it is on the wrist also like a rod and two coins.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for men and women is that you cut off all the attached parts, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine jumps through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the tension
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a part attached to the natural area, so that it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should dye the excess of the tentigene to your hand or with needles, and cut it lightly; do not go too deep, so that bleeding does not occur, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and for another part that grows at the mouth of the womb, and use it, and perhaps it becomes hard, and it resembles a horn, and for this reason the ancients called it the "horn sickness.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	So you must cut it as we have said about the tendon, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental due to illness that has come about; or it is caused by thick skin or thin or thick membranes, and formed perfectly in the middle, sides, below, or wherever; and it prevents conception and childbirth, and sometimes menstruation; and knowledge of this is through examination.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears close, you should seek it with your hands or a probe.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is of the subtle spleen and it is near the two thighs, hurry up, and do this: put your two index fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then extend the two thighs well, so that the subtle spleen becomes round and over the swellings; then take wool, and anoint it with oil, and place it on the spot, and have the woman lie with a man each day, so that she cannot become pregnant.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the spleen is hard and thick, then you must shave it with a spatula shaped like a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of new flesh, then suspend it with a lancet and cut it; and use blood-stanching medicines, such as quicksilver, dragon's blood, incense, all mixed with egg white; then apply a broad bandage to keep the wound from closing; and thus do this for a long time, and dress it with a linen cloth; then continue other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when flesh grows in the wound, it must be cut according to this method, unless there are infected abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an infected abscess that is in the wound, one should not touch it with iron.
des emorroides	hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins from which blood flows habitually, and when hemorrhoids become old, they turn black; and we have said in the division their similarities and signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and blackened areas, when they are fully in the wound and do not protrude to be felt, should not be treated with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the maw, which one can feel, are those whom one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Then you must put the woman in a cold house, then extend the altar with tongs and cut it at its roots, then sprinkle medicines that stop blood, such as aloes and dragon's blood and frankincense, and similar things; then place her feet to the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if bleeding comes, then make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and lard, and make a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him apply leeches to the back and breasts without piercing; then take wool, and moisten it in plantain juice or in elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, clean the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so it must be cut as I have said for the tumor; and then clean it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the jaws
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the jaws, such as ulcers and stone abscesses and herpes and thrush and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary then that I say in this treatise the hot abscess which comes on the jaw, which is not one of the abscesses gathered by the bow; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look whether the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but let it die down until the pain is calmed; and then make the patient sit on a chair, and have two small chairs where he leans, and rests on his back and brings his feet together behind the leg; and let his thighs be spread apart, and place his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good binding; then turn the bail towards the right side, and bring the instrument used to work the mouth of the jaw, from which comes the form hereafter; and it is necessary that when you bring this instrument, you first fix a rod in to know the depth of the jaw, so that what enters inside the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the jaw with cloths, so that the instrument does not distress him; and it must be that he places the tip of the instrument above, and that he taints the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open, and it is cut with a soft hand, one must cut at the head, to the spatule edge; and when the bowel is empty, then you should put in the wound tents moistened in rose oil, or in dried green oil; and place the tent far from the wound into the marrow's depth, and put on top of the marrow and on the swelling clean wool moistened in water or where mallows are cooked; then treat after two days with anointing suitable for this, until it is healed; and sometimes one lifts the marrow and the wound by a catheter of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lilies and long Solomon's seal cooked; then return to the anointing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound has penetrated into the marrow, then you must be careful not to use hot iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to recognize the signs of natural childbirth, and these signs are when you see the woman pressing down, and desires to smell the air: then the child hastens to come out forcefully; then you know that this childbirth follows the natural order, and it comes out head first, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, then you should gently press her belly so that the child comes out quickly; for when it comes up head first, the afterbirth comes with it, and the mother is cleansed of her excesses by proper cleansing; and those who come out otherwise do not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes it comes out on its feet, and the body or the shoulder or the hands come first, or it comes out belly first, or buttocks first, and by chance is turned on its neck, and in other bad positions; therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skilled in these matters, and beware of error and deceit, and I will show you all the positions and how one should assist them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes onto its head through natural passage, and the woman gives birth heavily, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a stool where the women hold her; and boil oil or fenugreek, and then the midwife places the small spatula, whose shape is as follows, between her hands:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and split the amnion, and cut to her nail so that the moisture inside runs out; and take hold of the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must enema the woman with a paste of fenugreek mixed with sesame oil; then make her sneeze and snort from condyse, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out weak, then you must reset them gently bit by bit; and if they cannot go in, then put the woman on a chair, and lift her feet up high; then stand the chair on the ground, and tie down the woman so she does not fall when standing; and if the hand cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut off the hands with the knife that was placed there before, and extract the child, and reset equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out feet first, then you must push it upwards; and then turn it bit by bit until it is aligned; then take one of the feet and stretch it bit by bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps up to the thighs, then it commands to grasp it and makes sneeze with condiments; if it is strong, may God will.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not go strong as we have said, then turn it little by little until it is according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it moves lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come strong as we have said, then take a mixture of altitude, and sesame oil, and dissolved gum, and grind all in the mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and strengthen this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to the ribs; and when she is moistened underneath, make the collar of myrrh for her, and put it underneath, and leave it an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and grasp her belly lightly, for now the infant jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the birth of the child upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, the midwife places her hands gently; then she leans it on its neck, and lets its feet hang down, and lays it on the bed; and bends its arms little by little, and then takes its hands to its belly, and removes the cushions underneath until it is positioned downwards; and if the child does not come out, she takes its feet and pulls forcefully, then lifts its belly up, and then puts her hands there; and brings out the child gently; and commands the woman to push as much as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the birth of the child who comes with one hand extended widely
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	One must plan to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, then have the woman stand and walk; if she cannot walk, then have her lie on the bed, and extend her legs properly; then administer the ointment I have described; and if she does not give birth, then have her sit on a chair, and continue trying to bring back the hand; and draw out the child according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and command that she pulls as much as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on its neck, and have its hands spread out, and its face turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	One must have the midwife hold her hand, then turn it little by little, and draw it out gently; and when it is straightened, apply the natural ointment of altitude and oil as we have said, then command that she move little by little; and once you have done this, have her sit on a chair, and command that she pulls; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this same manner to all the small intestine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes in this manner to all the small intestine, cut the small intestine with your nail until the moisture is emptied; and if the fetus can be on its face and on its neck, then cut it from the bud so that it is not retained, and kill the fetus; then put the child inside until you have placed it as it should be, and instruct the woman to grasp herself several times: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things and do not live much if they have any name; I know that they are multiplied, and are separated by the sieve which divides them, which is tied to the stump; and sometimes they come out as naturally as some eggs, just as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out forcefully, then treat them as we have said, and the cure should be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what it does; and act thus as it is worth moving towards salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IIII or V or VI or VII, or many up to XV, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious, and it is necessary that the healer know all this, for perhaps similar things happen; so do according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman for the dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to use manual work; then you must know if the woman is of sound health, and has no condition that would cause fear of death; then the woman must be laid on her back, and her shoulders inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the attendant should tie her in two parts, so she is fastened to the bed so that she does not move with the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils mixed with muslin of althea and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint both hands of the operator with these oils and these mixtures; then gently insert them into the womb, then search for the place where you should apply the hooks that are suitable for this purpose, and be careful if the child is positioned so that it comes down on its head; then insert the hooks in its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or forceps near the sides, and if the descent is on feet, insert them into the ankles and middle ribs; and you must hold the hook in your right hand, and place the curette between the fingers of your left hand, and gently apply it with all your hand, and insert the hook into one of these places that we have said until you reach the empty space; and this is the form of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then place against the other bone, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction be equal; and then stretch equally by moving from one side to the other, for the teeth to come out, and let the bones be toothed to hold the teeth, as is shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part of it remains, then anoint the healthy part with some of his fingers oiled, and insert them into that part, and pull the other part; and if any point remains, then place this bone in a higher position, and do this until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other and cannot be brought back due to constriction, then you must wrap it with a cloth until it comes out completely; then cut it at the joint of the palm or the wrist; and thus you should do the same for the other hand, and for both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the shoulder of the child is large and it is stuck in the birth canal, or there is a pointed head gathered at the top, then you must put the spatumile spine between your fingers, cut the head and extract the water; or you round it with the tool that is called «almidach», from which the form comes with the tools of the chapter that follows this one; and likewise do if the child has a large head naturally; and then pull out the bones with forceps, and if the shoulder jumps out and holds on to the forceps, then it should be split so that the moisture in the swelling can come out; and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the inflammation is on his feet, then the attraction is light, and the adjustment at the mouth of the ulcer is slight.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is strong in the belly or the breast, then you must stretch it with a cloth wrapped on the hand; and cut the belly or the breast until the moisture that is there runs out; and if other limbs are removed and the head remains, then the physician puts his hand into the depth of the ulcer and draws it to the mouth of the ulcer; then he puts one or two fingers in, and pulls strongly; and if the mouth of the ulcer is narrowed by a hot abscess that has come there, then you must not work on it, but you should administer moist and fatty things; and apply plasters, and sitz baths with softening and moisturizing water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the fetus is on its side, and you can make it straight, then apply what we have said for the living child; and if one cannot do so, then pull it out by parts, and leave nothing of the secondine.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, apply what we have said for hot abscesses that come in the marrow; and if bleeding occurs, then apply constricting water, and treat with other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb one fetus had been dead, then another was placed on top of it, and the other also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came upon the buttock, and swelled so much that it burst open, and began to severely putrefy.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat, and I pondered for a long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong attracting poultice, and an bone came out, and after some days others did as well.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I probed the wound, and pulled out more bones, until the woman was much better; and the woman lived for a long time thereafter, and there came out a little pus from the place; and I have recorded this chapter not only because when masters find strange things, they should take note to add aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the dislocated to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of the press, with which books are pressed; and it has two wheels at the two ends of the two shafts.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be finer than the restrictor, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft should be one inch wide, and the margin of the boards one inch, and in length one and a half palms; and between the two shafts should be two fittings of this same wood, which are fixed on one and the other side, half a palm long or a little more; and these two fittings are inserted into the mouth of the dislocation to open when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of pincers; and it should have at both ends two attachments, as you see, a palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the maw with all the instrument, make the woman sit on one bed, feet hanging down and legs spread, then put the two attachments together into the maw, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand at all the instrument as you have done with pincers equally, according to the quantity that you wish to open the mouth of the maw, until the uterus does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all perfected, and their forms are multiplied; and when the physicians have them prepared, the work is done more quickly, and they are more valuable to people according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	So do not despair of the instrument that you have prepared, for their necessity is not avoidable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained at childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, then make her sneeze with condiments, and hold your hands over her mouth and nose; and if she succeeds by this means, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make a hole in the lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamus, rue, anise, camomile, cassia lignea, and centory; all these herbs or some of them should be boiled in the pot with water over the fire; then place one end of a tube in the hole of the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the womb, and smoke until the vapors come inside the womb; then make her sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then the tendon springs quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and does not go out, then instruct the nurse to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or in marjoram plaster, and then apply it naturally, and seek the tendon; and when she has found it, take hold of it and stretch it little by little straightly so that the disorder does not fall during extraction; but it is necessary to move it lightly to right and left, and then pull; it will come out and unstick.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the opening of the disorder is very narrow, we have mentioned the treatment of sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not come out entirely as we have said, beware that you do not follow through with pulling; but it is necessary that what is at the opening of the disorder be tied to the thigh of the woman, then cleanse her with a tetrafarmacum enema; she will expel and reset, and it will come out; however, still when she expels, there comes a bad odor in the stomach and head, and hurts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So suitable fumigations are required for this: some of the ancients have experienced the fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of flowers and the secondina is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass resembling a cane, and one places the narrow end inside the body, and the wide ends over the fire; and let the fumigation be on the coals, and continue until it is spent, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the anus
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have a pierced anus, but it is stopped up with a fine membrane: so it is necessary for the nurse to pierce that membrane appropriately, and not use a sharp spatula, and be careful not to touch the sutures; then apply wool moistened in wine and oil, and continue the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will relapse, put a pin of lead in the hole, and leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this swelling comes from the adhesion of a wound or an abscess; it is necessary to cut that adhesion: then it should be treated, as we have said about the pin of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come below the anus are nodules and swelling that appear near the anus or in the space of two parts, and there is one fistula or more; and when this nodule is old, it works, and often emits white or thin pus, and sometimes these fistulas are perforated; they are recognized by the fact that something comes out during defecation or flatulence when the patient evacuates, and occasionally some of them may leak.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that reach as far as the bladder, and up to half of the penis; they extend as far as the hip joint, and up to the knot of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula penetrating to the fundament and not penetrating: it is that you put your index finger in the fundament, and insert a fine needle of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has curvature, then insert a thin lead probe or horsehair until you feel the probe or the hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge of excrement, wind, or worm as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; do not hasten to cleanse it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula extends all the way to the bladder or to the urinary conduit, the urine leaks out, and cannot be sealed by medications.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And if it extends to the joint of the thigh, then the pain reaches that place; if there is no curvature and the source of the pain around it, then urine immediately flows out, and neither medicine nor ointment can seal it; and in these penetrating fistulas, there is no cure other than labor, and the foolishness of those who intervene is vain.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In those that are not penetrating and not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on their back; then lift their legs up to their thighs, and incline their thighs towards their belly; then insert a probe of lead or bronze if there is curvature, until you know where the pain comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must put your index finger there, and if you sense that the tent has pierced it; and whether uncovered or not where you feel between your finger the surface or the flesh, then you know that it is perforated; do not work at it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	They say that sometimes it can be healed well, but this happens rarely; and the aid that one does, is to heat the fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as was previously mentioned; and put it very hot into the fistula until it reaches near the anus; and do this two or three times until you know that the foul flesh is burned, which looks like a bird's feather; then clean it with moistened cloths in butter, until that flesh comes out, then cleanse it with an ointment that heals and binds the flesh.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this is the case, it cannot be healed otherwise; and if the tent enters, and does not reach the bone at the base, and there is a thick cover of flesh or sinus between your finger and the tent, and you see the fistula under this cover from the core; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push the tent forward immediately, and cauterize afterward until it reaches the head of the tent; the tent will be freed and fall out; then clean those corrupted flesh that look like a bird's feather, and leave nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound swells and forms between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicinal substances.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two good things: that is to know, the closure of these burned areas joined, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then treat wet tents with butter or crushed things until the pus flows out, and the burned area in the pus comes out; then treat the wound with hot ointments that soften hard flesh, and are the medicines dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up from the bottom of the anus and is distant from the body, put your finger in the anus and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent and between two is the tissue or the sinus or flesh, where it is close to piercing, there should be no force but way of faith and hope, through the administration of one of the three ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put tents and treat it as before; do not go too deep that you do not cut the lining which holds the anus, and the excretions come out unwillingly; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it after it is cut near the anus, either by tent or by another sharp instrument; then cleanse that diseased flesh which is in the wound as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and keep the fistula in the part outside the anus: this will be a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and it is when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is at the side of the anus near the skin above, then take a probe pierced at the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you twist the thread around two, and insert the probe with all the thread into the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced at the edge of the anus inside, then withdraw the thread from that perforation, as you insert your finger into the anus; and pull the end of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and bind one to the other, and leave it for one day or two; and sometimes tighten it until the thread cuts through the tissue that is between them, and they fall out; then treat the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not burst, then make it burst in all ways that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to cut so deeply for the suture and then clean it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spatumile spine used to make the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what should not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are according to two manners: they are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there can be small and large ones, and they bleed immediately; and there can be one or more, and they are outside the anus and at the head of the anus; but those which are outside have little moisture, and they also contain a bit of yellow bile or a bit of blood, and have the color of the flesh. The treatment for those who have them inside the anus is that you instruct the patient to strain as if going to the chamber, so that the anus comes out, and then the threads appear; then hurry and grasp it with forceps, or hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at its roots; and if the uncinate cannot hold due to moisture, then take them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of linen; and pull them out with your hands, then cut them, and sprinkle some warm powders that are like cautery on top; or you cauterize them as is said in the chapter about cautery, then treat them further until they heal. And if the anus cannot come out, then give the patient a harsh and rough purgative to wash what is inside the anus so it can come out clearly; when the patient strains, and if the threads are outside the anus, the treatment is light; that you take them with your fingernail or forceps, cut them, then treat them as we have said until they heal, and fear incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So you must administer the stitch in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it through a needle, and then pull the thread above and pierce the needle from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and so let it be wide; and tighten the thread properly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do this for all the others, and leave one to drain the excess blood; then place over the wound a cloth moistened in rose oil or in ointment, and put on the wound, and instruct the patient to rest; and then let it be until they drop, and when they have fallen out, clean them with ointment and other treatment, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the dryness of the dung or wound
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Very often there is dryness of phlegm in the intestines, and by constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must scrape at the tip of a spit or with your nail the bark above, which should not be moistened; then clean it until it is sodden as it should be; and if it cannot become sodden, then begin the shaving more forcefully than before, until it bleeds much, and is skinned; then clean it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of the trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small faulty appearance around the body, and it spreads very quickly; and sometimes it is found by cold, and it is felt like death from trembling, and it affects the whole body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a quill from a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and put that quill on the wart, so that the circle surrounds the wart completely; then turn your hand all around the quill until you cut all around the wart, and place it perfectly, and pluck the wart from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a needle of brass or iron according to this form, and let it be thin below and sharp above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce, to hold the flame steady, and to press the flame And if you wish, cauterize the wart, as it is described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	about the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes a clyster is made of silver or gold, or melted tin or lead; and sometimes these substances are made small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are administered in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large clyster is wide on top, where the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there should be an opening where the belly is tied, as you see, and the end should be pierced inside; and it should have two holes on one side, and one hole on the other; and the belly where one puts the medicines should be made of an animal bladder or parchment, and should be pierced all around with small holes, and there should be one inch of space between each hole, then insert a strong thread of raw linen through ten or more times around, and gather the belly like a goat's; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument at the front with a strong thread, then perform the clyster; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg white, or similar thing, then put it in gently; then the minister grips it with both hands together until it is all shut, then withdraws the clyster, and lifts the patient's legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, holds it back as much as he can; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysterize in a disease of flux from the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, restart it until he is purged.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the anus, or an abscess, then let the clyster be as fine as for a child; and this is the form of the fine clyster on which the skin should be restrained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicine, according to the fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made by, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the throwing of stones, and the cutting of sword and knife, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar things; or that they are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that lies on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, for the remembering will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take note if it is from a stone or similar objects, and the skin is entirely ruptured and the wound is large, and you doubt the formation of a hot abscess: then have it bled immediately from the cephalic vein especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be opposite to the wounded part; and purge the patient of excess wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not bleed, then reduce his food intake, and let him drink no wine nor eat meat; and apply to the wound, if hot abscesses come, cotton moistened only in rose oil or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then apply on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood and not moved by air, powder, which I will mention a little later; and if the sun has dried it out, then apply some ointments until he is healed.
