Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword cut and similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by hand, then bring them together by stitching, just as I will say for abdominal wounds, about the suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and can, and holds no more than a little, then cut it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as heads and cooked wheat, also like pulse, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotten skin, and it does not reach the bone, then cut out all the rot and throw it away, then clean it; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be stopped by medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it dislodged, then secure it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: it is that you put in this powder which seals as soon as the fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live coals three parts, and powder them finely, and apply to the wound, and press it strongly, until it dries well and adheres to all its blood; then bind it well, and leave it without loosening, unless it swells; for you do not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes this is done with coals alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but the fire has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn has moved the wound, especially in this state, one does not put this powder on it; but put some digestible ointments on it, or flour of barley made with water and honey until it gives pus; then cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you hereafter about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other method but to leave the treatment and not apply anything restraining, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their connection with us is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as hot washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber also washed in sweet water, and other minerals according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with blood, pierce it at the lowest point; and if an artery is cut and bleeding occurs, expose it, tie it off, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut or the conduit is damaged through which food passes, sew the conduit onto the canal of the throat, do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural form; then bind it appropriately, leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it heals; and if the wound has pressed into the bone, remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, extract all that you can, and those you cannot have, leave them until the wound becomes gangrenous, and clear and relieve the discharge; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then look to see if wind issues forth when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder at the first hour, nor bind it tightly because the blood does not clot properly and returns to the heart, killing the patient; but apply an attractive ointment and bandage it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, then place old cotton in the wound to draw out moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wounded side for three days, or four, or more; there will be no spasm, nor trembling of heart, nor strangling breath; and when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it then with bandages and other treatments, until he is healed; and if she cannot heal, and acts, then know that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, whether on the front or back, treat it with what is in front; if it is large, by suturing; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has chipped pieces, then wash the wound, and pull out the splinters if they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound fester to lighten the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgement is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the abdomen is large and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines come out, causing intrusion of air; and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a large one, because one delays in properly placing the intestines back inside if they are not placed immediately; for the intestines swell as soon as they feel cold, making them harder to return, thus a medium-sized wound is better because the intestines can be more easily returned to their place than with others. And know that the rupture of the abdomen occurs in four ways: two common sutures happen at the suture of the abdomen, and the other wounds of the body have two other specific sutures which are common to other wounds; however, they are more specific to the suture of the abdomen, and I will speak of each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestine comes out, and it is difficult to put back, this is due to one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or soft cloth with lukewarm water only, or you boil in water squinant and cypress and spike, and wet the intestine until the swelling is removed; and sometimes wine that restrains does this, and it is better than alone for reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water in which fennel and mallows have been boiled, for by this means the entrance is eased slightly; and if it cannot enter, cut a little of the wound with the instrument with which we cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is better than the incision, which should not be made without great necessity; and here is the instrument to make the incision: cut inside in the curvature and do not go out, and see here the form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is widened, and the intestines jump out, then reset them according to their natural form in their proper place if you can, for this is worth doing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is wide, and it is in the part below the belly, then you must have the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, then raise the head and chest higher than the parts below, and likewise if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, place your attention so that the wounded part be higher than the other; and thus you must administer what I say in large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds use what is prepared for you, then take in your hands one tender minister who sews up the entire rupture with his hand and brings together the lips; and this is the common way of stitching, which is that you take a needle or more according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound an inch of space, and stick in a needle with it having strong thread; and pierce both sides of the skin with both sides of the sinew, which is below the skin inside, until you make it pierce that part, and bring together both ends of the sinew four altogether; then stretch a double thread around the needle from two parts, then bring together both sides of the wound fittingly, and then leave an inch of space, and stick in another needle; then tie the end of the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what needles you need until all the wound is restrained; and let the needles be medium, between fine and thick, for the fine needles cut up all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot enter well: therefore they should be medium; and it does not befit to push the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and work on the wound before the healing; then cut off the ends of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient in sleeping, and put tents or cloths at the ends of the needles to hold them firmly, and leave them until the wound is healed; this way of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, for there fits one needle or two. The second stitch is common, which is that you bring together both sides of the skin and both sides of the sinew together on a needle with it having medium strong thread; and when you have pierced all these four parts together, then continue the needle to the part where you began in the way clothes are sewn; put an inch of space between each stitch as thick as one small finger. This stitch know men, and I stitched a wound that a man had on his stomach which was cut by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and two palms of intestines came out, and the wound was in the middle of the stomach.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been outside for 24 hours, and the wound was sutured up to 15 days, and I treated it, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of sewing: take the needle and push it from the outer part to the inner; when it has pierced straight through the center, then hold the head of the needle where you have sewn, and make it pierce again from the inner part to the outer; the meaning of this stitch is that you sew just as a tanner works with skins, leaving one side out once and then taking it up again, until the stitching is fully completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of suturing, which Galen properly described, is as some do, who bring the two parts together naturally, and apply one end of the surface to the other end, in such a way: stick a needle at the end of the wound that is closer, and pierce only that place, leaving both ends of the surface; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part to the inner part, at two ends of the surface; then pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner part, at two other points of the wound which are on the opposite side; and this is the crudest manner of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this word, and some testify to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread; and one must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather straps; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suturing is more difficult than at other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, although the fire has moved it, then reset the intestines, and the cut; then put on powder to heal flesh, and if the fire has moved it, then put on some ointment that is present until the wound drinks; stitch the thread, and let the sifac and mirach be soldered; then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to expel drink, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no need of other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you fear that the wound may communicate with the principal members, then you must moisten light wool in tempered hot oil or in rose oil, and place it around the armpits and under the arms; and if he feels pain or putrefaction in boils, which often happens, then cleanse them with warm black wine, and likewise if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is because of the thinness of the veins that are there, and due to the delicacy of the entire body, and its closeness in nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the hernia comes out of the wound, reset it as you would with the intestine while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned green or black, then you must tie the place that is black so no further bleeding occurs, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the tie, and let the two sides hang from below the wound up above to lighten the extraction when the hernia falls out, and the wound draws together.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are round, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, because I saw that a man was wounded in the belly with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and excretions and wind came out; I put care according to what I could, and did not stop subtlety until he was healed, and the opening was sealed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it sealed, I feared that the patient might have trouble in his belly; and he had no trouble, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimentors said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be tied in such manner: take pins with large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the pin has opened its mouth, place it over both edges so that it holds its mouth closed; then cut off the head, and this stays so that it cannot come undone, then put another pin after in the same way as before, until the entire wound is bound up; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	These heads are burned in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can sew the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of this intestine thread which is very thin, and then tie to this thread the fine linen thread twisted, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and keep it together at the rupture; and this method of stitching firmly is not different from according to the way of trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the major intestines, there is no skill or knowledge except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of the fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it awakens, is generally called a "fistula," and especially when it is hairy and runs pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth a false and hard knot, white, where there is no pain, and it is also hairy like the feathers of a bird; and sometimes it discharges clear pus, and other times thick; sometimes little, and other times enough; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, is due to none but one of the nine causes: namely, by the smallness of the blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the site is porous, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence; or due to the property in the region where digestion is slow, and health comes late, and swollen by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now you must know the treatment of fistula which is done by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistula occurs in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or on the surface, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or at the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet; and there is such that comes to the principal part of the member and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the places I have mentioned, and you have confidence in its treatment, and you wish to know it, then take a probe of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, then cut it; and if the fistula is twisted, then search it with a delicate probe of lead, for lead can bend around the twists; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot explore it well with probes, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for moisture will run from one opening to another and cleanse it; then cut it wisely as much as you can so that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and this should be done carefully, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when pressed by your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you truly know the location of its presence, and if it is far from joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any places that I have told you, then cut it according to what I have said, and remove the pus and corrupted flesh inside; and then treat it until it heals, and if the fistula is very deep straight ahead, then cut completely as much as you can, then place moistened probes with healing medicine, and push them to the head of the fistula so that the medicine corrodes the excess left at the bottom; and then apply ointments that promote healthy flesh until it heals; and if it does not heal by this method, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not trouble the main limbs as we have said; and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, then cut until all the corruption is removed, then treat with things that heal flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed and begins to ooze as before, know that you have not gone deep enough: so expose and scrape until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the area; and if it heals in this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted and you can extract it with tongs, then pull it out with the appropriate tool for this, and if there are many bones, extract them all, do not leave even one; and if moisture works against you and there is no mistake nor fear, cut away both moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, then put on the wound a substance promoting putrefaction, and leave until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then they will have the bones more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, then cleanse only up to the corruption until all blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of the corrupted, coming up to the marrow of the bone; you must saw and cut right up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you of an ulcer that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something that came inside the body, so that the matter came to the leg, and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it; but the doctors, by their folly, worked on it until the abscess opened, and much material corroded out, and became an ulcer, and many leaks developed from which all kinds of bowels and moisture of the body poured out; and many doctors treated it for about two years, and there was no wise person in the art of hands until I was called to it, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being cured, and what came out through the leaks with great corruption; and the body of the young man turned red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I placed a tent in one of these perforations, and then searched all the perforations, and found that one came opposite the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the perforations until I uncovered part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced; the corruption reached inside to the bone. I removed what appeared to be the corrupted bone, thinking there was no other corruption except for that which I had taken out; I began to heal the wound with poultices over a long time, but it would not close. Then I started again and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, so I scraped and removed it, then tried to close the area; but I could not until I cut around nearly an inch of the bone, and entirely through its mass, then applied medicines; it healed and closed quickly, and there was no need to begin the work again except for the patient's weakness, which they could not bear, and the fear of death that I had for them.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation he often bled, but he was entirely healed, and in place of the bone a hard flesh grew, and it was of good disposition and had no harm nor contrary effect whatsoever, neither coming nor going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be sutured in this manner: take a thread, and tie it at the head of the exposed bone, and command someone to pull it up; and place another thread of wool thicker than the first thread on the flesh that is over the bone, and stretch the head so that you draw out the corrupted flesh underneath, and expose the flesh where you wish to sew, so that the suture does not injure the flesh; and place a hot iron or a board under the bone to cut away the corrupted flesh; and one must sew as much as can be seen and felt of the corruption, and sew again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover all the flesh; then put the ember underneath, and then sew from one side to the other the corruption, and let the sewing be as long as the corruption itself, just as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, cut off the corrupted joint, and sew the bone where it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, then there is no other remedy but to cut; and if the corruption is at the wrist of the hand or the ankle of the foot, this thing is very difficult, but nonetheless you must investigate that corrosion, how it appears to you; and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but that the vein or the nerve does not oppose you; and know that the incisors and the saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and their fineness, and their size and their smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to equip each kind of work with its tool; and know that the work will show you the tool that you need according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of diseases; so consider the tool that you need according to what it should be.
dou feu	of the fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder rots either from within or due to lack of force; and when you have treated that corruption with medicine but it does not help, then one must cut off the limb up to the place where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes death by this means or by the mischief, which is greater, of lacking a limb; and the sign is that the limb turns black as if burned by fire, and after the blackness appears, the corruption spreads member by member and throughout the body; thus hurry to cut it off, and if it is due to the bite of venomous creatures such as sea scorpion and basilisk and similar, and the corruption is at the tip of the toe, then cut it off, and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, cut at the joint so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut below the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and no remedy avails except for the amount of his strength; and all thus do when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes in the first joint, cut beyond the other joint; and if it comes on the foot, cut off the entire foot; and if it rises into the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to death; and the method of cutting or sawing the member is that you tie above and below, and have one minister hold one tie down, and another minister the other tie up, and you separate the flesh which is between the two ties by a spatula wide, until the bone be uncovered; then cut or saw it, and put on each side a linen cloth so that the saw does not touch the healthy place, and cause in the patient another injury and hot abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, then quickly cauterize the place, or put some binding powders on it; then return to your treatment until it is completed, then bind the wounded limb with an appropriate bandage, and care for it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: he had a blackening that seemed like fire's burning, and this corrosion first came on his toe of the foot, until it would spread over the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hurried to cut off the foot, and was healed; and long afterward the corrosion returned on the thumb of his hand, and he came to me, and I put repelling things on after cleansing the body, and could not stop the corruptions; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, for I had hope of repelling the matter; and also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the man's strength was weak; and he lost all hope, returned to his home, hurried to cut off his hand, and was healed; and I have this recounted only so that it is known that one should act otherwise, when necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in a cartilaginous area and remains for so long that it makes a great gathering of pus; then it rots and breaks open, and the pus jumps out, and the place becomes as if empty; and the skin above is as delicate as fine drapery, and does not extend to the bone or to the nerve, and such disease is called «sain», and is not called «fistula»; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone perfectly, then it is called «fistula»; and you must cut all around that skin even when it is delicate as fine drapery; and its corruption does not stop.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you fear that the skin will burn, and the corruption is not yet perfect, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with an enema in this way: look if the breast is large, and the pus that comes out has a foul smell, then enema it with Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take hellebore, oil, and litharge equally, and cook them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; and then take of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and enema the breast, and tie up the opening; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then extract it by squeezing; do this many times until the breast is cleansed, and the filth is removed; and sometimes it is enema with lye water when this medicine is not available, and take vine wood ash and pour water over it, then strain it, and use it as an enema until you know that the breast is well cleaned; if the patient cannot bear it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor the lye water, then enema it with water and honey where there is a bit of ground litharge mixed in; or enema it with a mixture of honey and wine, for honey has the property to cleanse and wash, and wine makes the abscess burn; and when you have done this, and you believe that the breast is well cleansed, then enema it with what makes flesh grow in it, and take diaphoretic plaster and mix it with rose oil and wine; or enema it with some medicines and ointments of which I have mentioned their properties in the chapter on ointments; if the opening of the breast is small, and the enema tube cannot enter, then widen it a bit with an iron, and put some of the Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment inside so that it widens; if the wound is too large, sew it up and leave only one place where the enema can enter, and if the opening that discharges pus is on top, then cut it at a lower spot.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the pus is perfect, it does not allow flesh to grow; and if you cannot cut under the breast as much as you wish, then arrange in such a way that the pus flows to the lowest point possible, for when the pus is perfect, it does not allow flesh to grow and if you cannot cut under the breast as much as you wish, then arrange in such a manner: so that the pus runs lightly downwards, and leave nothing of the pus; and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and stretch over the linen cloth that covers all the wound; then cut forcefully at the narrow part of the breast slightly wider than the first, then extend an ointment above another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it over the wound of the breast to lighten the pus, and do not remove the large cloth except once after many days; and that which is on the opening of the breast, remove often to remove the pus, and know what flows from the pus, whether it is venom or little or much, or digested or indigested; and be wary if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been spread in such a way and you see the nature that rises on the opening of the wound, then know that the breast starts to heal and health approaches; and then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast discharges undigested fluid after many days, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle pus forms after a long time, do not despair of the health, for recovery approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people whose wounds take a long time to granulate, and of those who do the opposite; and if undigested fluid shoots from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healing; and if the breast delays in healing and is widespread, then apply moist substances with drying properties, such as diaphoretic ointment, for it contains a large portion of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take diaphoretic ointment, and make it with rose oil, and sprinkle old wine equally on the substance; then cook it and use it; and this same thing works better when honey is thickened, when diaphoretic ointments are not present, or you take balm and aloe and frankincense, and grind them, and powder them over the honey while it is over the fire; then glue the drapery, and stretch it over the breast, and sometimes aristologe longe and roots of celestial lilies, which are also like wheat flour and chalk; and use simple or compound herbs: grind them, make a powder, put it on the honey I have mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and not cured by this treatment, then know that the corruption is perfect, and affects the bone, or hard parts, or ligaments; treat it with fistula treatment, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger of the hand, or of the foot, or sometimes arises in other digits; and when it becomes old, and no attention is taken, then comes the hot abscess, and it runs and casts pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes it eats through entirely; and the corrosion goes up to the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the joint of the digit swells wide, and its color turns pale.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut with an iron all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is much help if the bone is sound, and the nail is sound; and if the nail presses the flesh inwards, and it begins to hurt, and wounds it, then you must put the edge under the nail that pierces the flesh, and lift it up, and cut that flesh subtly and lightly, and apply on the remaining of the flesh medicines burning and corrosive to remove all; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and remove it thoroughly, for as long as the corrupted bone remains there, it cannot heal; and if you see it must be corrupted, then cut it into one of the directions as was said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is infected and inflamed and causes great pain, you must first cleanse it; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula by cutting across above, and take care that the cut does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the swelling of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The dislocated finger that occurs in some men is entirely fleshy, and sometimes it has bones, and occasionally there is a nail, and some are born at the root of the joint, where the birth is in some ways of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any knot of the finger does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the finger sometimes moves; the size of the fleshy one is slight, in such a manner: cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to treat: be careful with cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In him who is born with a hernia in the buttock, you must first cut away the flesh roundly to the bone, then cut the bone to an appropriate seam, then cleanse it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The webbing that comes between the fingers is due to birth, or by the joining of a wound, or by burning of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut that webbing so the fingers return to their natural forms; then place between two cloths or oiled rags that they do not join together; or you put between two pieces of fine linen until the joints are joined as is proper.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If webbing comes between any of his fingers and the palm, then cut that webbing as is proper.
des vils	of the villages
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	There are large swollen veins full of melancholic superfluities, which come into many parts of the body; and it happens more in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him a purgation of bile, and then heal him with basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is according to two methods: one is that they are cut, and black blood is drawn out; and the other method is that you open the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done in this manner: first wash the leg with very hot water until the thick skin becomes fine, then bandage the patient’s leg from above the thigh down to below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two or three, with a wide incision, then elevate and draw out the black blood by hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the strength of the patient can withstand; and then bind it up, and instruct him to nourish himself on meat that increases black bile; and repeat the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full, which is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The lifting of it is according to this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put him in a bath, and wash the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, heat it by fire, and then cut straight along the vein from the long part to the head of the knee, or in the area below at the ankle; then work the skin with a lancet, and scrape the vein on both sides until it appears when felt; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white thread; then push the needle underneath, so that it is lifted from the skin, then scrape it slightly with the lancet, then cut in another place three times; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it with the needle as you have done, and paint it with another lancet as you did first; then cut another length, or more if needed, then lift it, and cut at the toe of the foot, then pull and lift up to the second length; then extract from length to length until it comes out completely, then cut; and if you cannot pull and lift it, put a needle with a strong double thread, and pull and pull, and put under the needle, and turn your hand one way and another until it comes out; and beware that it does not break, for if it breaks, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and harm comes to the patient; and when you have completely extracted it, put on the place of the wound wool soaked in wine and rose oil; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the skin is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it obliquely, but do not cut it off; and pull it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron with which one cuts the skin is curved, and it does not cut through, so that it does not cut the vein; and it is of thick curvature, for if it were finer, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil war
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This war is bred in the legs, in hot areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in land that has no moisture; and sometimes it arises in other places besides the legs, and this happens due to the corruption that comes beneath the skin, just as serpents and worms come within the body, bred between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then changes the color, and begins the vein to forcefully issue out, like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein is open, you must wrap around a piece of cloth from one and a half to two fingers wide, tie it, and leave the cloth hanging on the leg, and every time a point comes out too much, wrap it around the cloth again, and tie it; and if it is too long, cut off part of it, wrap the remainder, and do not cut at its root until it is all out; for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and putrefaction in that place, and a bad illness; therefore, it must be treated little by little until the end, leaving nothing in the body; and sometimes this vein, when treated, can be five palms long or ten, and one man came to me once, from whom it came out ten palms long, and when you cut it, make one incision at the opening, pierce it to the bottom so that everything comes out; then empty the matter inside, and apply healing medicines to prevent putrefaction for some days, then treat it as abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes at this vein there are fewer rains, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or by the foot, and much fluid comes out, and from which it jumps rains; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that arise between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "disease of the ox," because it often occurs to oxen, and it is a small worm that arises between skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body going up and down, and one can feel it well as it moves from member to member, until it bursts through the skin where it goes, and comes out forcefully; and it is engendered by the putrefaction of certain humors, just like worms and snakes and earthworms and ascarides in the stomach; and there is fear of its malice, for when it travels throughout the body, and ascends to the head, and reaches the eye, by chance it may enter, and destroy the eye; and this often happens.
