Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you want to cure and extract it, one cannot do so unless it moves: therefore then you must tie the area above and below with a strong bond tightly, then cut over and extract forcefully, and if the worm is embedded in the flesh, and you don’t find it, then cauterize with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it causes is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the head close to the eye, hold firmly below it the eyelid tightly, then cut over, and extract forcefully; and it is necessary for the patient to use purging of body with solutive medicines for the bad putrefied humors, and consume meat that prevents putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and then moves from member to member; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and right after, I saw it rise like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, just as quicksilver moves from one place to another; the pain left that spot and settled on the shoulder, and then shortly after ran throughout the body until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it was now circling around her body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how it moved so from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had seen many who wished to move the pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins exposed, and for this reason the constrained wind appeared; and it does not appear according to this reasoning to those who are plethoric, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you wish to treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then apply something on top and below quickly, and then cut so that the constrained wind comes out from that place; and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat it with what expels winds, such as foul pills, and pills of theriaca, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their forms and according to the places of the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and barbed ones, and welded ones; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and the one that falls in any limb falls in two ways: either in a principal member it lodges, such as brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls in any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you about later, appears: then you should refrain from extracting this arrow, for death often follows; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not embedded deeply, then extract it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and the cerebral fluid which is on top of the brain spills out, is when there is scotoma and bleeding and dizziness and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasms and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is a discharge without force from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps speech and voice are lost; and from the wound white moisture resembling pus flows out, and also like cooked meat juice; and if this sign appears to you, then be cautious with the treatment, and extract the arrow if it is inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it hits the heart is that it is near the left breast, and it feels as if it were fixed in something hard, not empty; and perhaps the arrow moves like pus, and black blood flows out, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting: then know without doubt that death is impending.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that is stuck in the throat is that without fail foam comes from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the lung, it is near the ribs; and it causes great anguish and great pain and sighing; and all the limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps some undigested flesh comes from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the abdomen, and no pus comes out through the intestines, there is no hope in the treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps and comes out forcefully, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the arm and the spine and the wrist and the thigh and the legs, and similar members, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow struck him in the arm at the root of the nose: I probed it and drew it out from another side beneath the fat of the ear, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And draw out at once an arrow that fell into the fat of the eye beneath the parchment below, and the arrowhead was embedded, and could not reach the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears; the youth was healed, and no ill accidents came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And draw out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I seized the barbs, and maneuvered so much that I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And draw out an arrow from the man, which had pierced his belly, and I thought he would die; and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut into the arrow, manipulated it, drew it out forcefully, and he had no ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man to whom an arrow struck the back, and the wound was sealed over; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change its natural disposition, nor found harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you see another man to whom an arrow struck his face, and the wound was sealed; and he remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And extract an arrow from the man of the king’s princes, which had fallen in the middle of his nose, and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was entirely embedded. I was called for treatment after it had been three days since it fell.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	And I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I wanted it to enter a very fine tent, and I did not feel it; and he felt pricking and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I put on a drawing and digestive plaster to prevent swelling; and the head of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the plaster for several days, and reopened the wound again, and the patient remained this way for a long time until he felt the arrow one day inside his chest; and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put corrosive medicine on the wound for several days until it was open, and I probed it, feeling the head of the arrow that had settled in place; then I applied more corrosive medicine to the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow appeared clearly; and he survived well over four months, after which I widened the wound enough to insert the tongs, and moved it from side to side, but could not remove it; then I continued to refine and devise various methods of extraction until one day I grasped it with properly made tongs, as will be detailed at the end of this chapter, so that I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physicians judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it then, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	And I have told you the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you apply your care to what I do not say, for the books cannot take everything into account; but wise masters compare well on a very small thing, and upon what is present and lacking, find new work, and new instruments, to counter the unfamiliar things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not leave the members where they are fixed in two ways: either through the place where they enter, or from another part; and those that come out through the place where they enter are arrows entering into their flesh, and sometimes coming out the same way.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump out now, leave it until the flesh around rots and the discharge is alleviated; and likewise if it is embedded in the bone and cannot come out, leave it thus for some days, moving it each day; then it jumps out, and if it still does not jump out, pierce around all the way through the fine shaft until the area around widens, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head and reaches one of the brain's chambers, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned befall the patient: do not extract it, but leave it until it becomes equal after some days, for if the arrow reaches as far as there, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not fixed only in the bone and does not reach the surface, and the patient remains for some days without ill effect, then the instrument should be used to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then apply tar around it as I have told you; then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in a part of the body where it cannot be seen, search for it throughout the tent; and if you feel it, extract it with an appropriate instrument; and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, cut until the wound is larger; and extract the arrow if you can, and if it has ears by which it clings, remove the flesh that is embedded in two parts as much as you can, then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; be careful not to break the arrow, which would make extraction more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then leave it until the skin around is stretched, then pull it out, for the extraction will be eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood goes against you, then follow what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and be careful of cutting the nerve and vein, and use ingenuity on how you can pull out the arrow without peril, whether quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position he was in when the arrow hit him, for this is the greatest aid there could be, and if you cannot, then put him according to what the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another side, where some part of it is visible, or the skin is swollen in such a way that it can be seen or clearly felt: cut then over it until the forceps can grasp it, and then extract it: thus it shall now come out.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly until it enters into the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it and begin the extraction again until it comes forth; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, push all the shaft; and if the shaft falls and you want to administer piecemeal, then administer the instrument with hair so that the tip of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then push out, and if the arrow is hairy, use an instrument with a pointed end entering in to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, then you must cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls on the bone or in the belly or at the bladder or at the ribs, and it is close, and you can cut above, then cut; and beware of cutting the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if need be; and care for it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the pincers used to remove arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and you see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form of the hair tip is also like the feather of a bird, to place at the tip of the arrow, as shown here the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tongs for piercing and pressing is here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	the veins of the body commonly
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which one recovers, of which sixteen are in the head, to wit: two that are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the temples appearing; and the two veins that are in the tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two guindeges that are in the neck; and the two veins that are on the upper lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and the common people call it the "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "faste", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and the common people call it the "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and the common people call it the "vein of the belly", and it is above the flexor muscle, and it is the one from which one bleeds, which clearly appears on the elbow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the bend of the elbow on the left side, and the second saphenous which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is at the ankle on the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The swelling of veins behind the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines; and the qualities of swelling as I tell you are that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then have the patient squeeze his neck tightly like a screw, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent places from the head: catch them therefore with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, mark it; then take the lancet, and push it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upwards, and cut both the skin and the vein well twice across, and let as much blood flow as you see fit; then tie it off and bind it, until it is bled out; and I have already said about the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The inflammation of the two arteries that are in the temples is good for old migraines, sordes, and customary ophthalmia, and for the flow of watery tears to the eyes; and the quality of the bleeding is as I say: and it is that the patient strains his neck so that the two veins appear clearly; and feel the pulse under your finger, then incise; then place your thumb on top of the vein above your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath, and raise the vein up, and cut it, just as you did with the other two veins, and let blood according to your need; then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton; then tightly bandage it, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The vein of the forehead is as valuable as the cephalic vein for old face diseases, and for migraines, and for redness; and its quality is such that the patient twists his neck so much that the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "excavator", whose form is here:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press firmly with your hand, or with something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you wish; then release the patient's neck, and tie off the vein until it is sealed and sometimes the work is done with a wide bandage.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not appropriate for the lancet to be too sharp; and cut across the vein, because the bone is close, and by chance the lancet might break when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The swelling of the two veins that are in the two temples helps the eyes, and the mange, and the redness, and the yellowing in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the quality of its swelling is that the patient strains his neck by twisting some band as before; then he bleeds it, and let the bleeding be sideways, a bit long from the flame a bit wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are delicate, it may break; then let the blood flow as much as you need, and then bind cotton on top, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	Bleeding the vein of the nose is good for water retention, and for stubborn sores, and for facial diseases, such as migraine and redness that comes upon the face, especially when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient strains his neck, then pulls his nose with your left hand, and take a delicate long flame, and insert it between the lips in the space which is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open easily here, and the blood will now start to flow; and do not go too deep, let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for a night, for it heals very quickly; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of the two binders helps with the tightness of the bridle, and at the beginning of mixology, and for many illnesses, and for impetigo, and for corrosives, and for herpes, and estiomenes; and the quality of the salve is that the patient stretches his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing on the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then apply the vein of the long one a bit widely, then draw blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then do likewise in the other vein, then untie the bandage, and bind both veins moderately so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, until the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the swelling of the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The swelling of the veins of the upper lips aids in phlegm in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and cracks in the lips, and from the nose and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the procedure for the swelling is to sit the patient in front of you, and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by their black color, and by the small black veins around them: cut both then, and if you do not recognize them and you are in doubt, cut the largest one on each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the swelling under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The swelling of the veins that are under the tongue comes after the swelling of the cephalic vein, and it is at the narrow part of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the sweller is that the patient sits between your hands facing the sun, and he lifts his tongue, and looks underneath on each side a black vein: then bleed one and the other, but do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the arm that are commonly bled are bled according to two methods: either by pricking with a broad martian blade, or with a fine olive-shaped blade like cutting edges, and it is called "anesil"; and they are broad and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The first form of the flame MARTIN is much renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins filled with thick and visible blood, and which contain thick and turbid blood; and this is the form of the olive-colored flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more finely pointed, and it is for healing the fine veins where there is fine yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The healing of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen; and it is necessary for the healer to heal wisely, and to beware of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, then it must be stopped, as I have said; and the flames should not be pressing but cutting like an ax.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open clearly, then you must extract it and change another one; or if you want any vein from it, or you incise in place of it a vein amidst the arm: it opens clearly; and cut it with an ax-like flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the site of the incision, then first you must bind the arm, touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the spot, and then tie up the arm, and cut the vein with an ax-like flame; and beware that you do not hit the artery when you see the spot swell, for it is the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rise up like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery: then hurry, and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger when the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind his arm, leave it thus, and let not the patient move it; and be full of fear, and do not move it until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding does not stop, and it overpowers you, and the medicines are not at hand, then cut the artery where it opens, for the head of the retractors; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a bark of fennel, and split it, and take one of the halves and bind it well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, then treat it as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and the stopping of bleeding is not difficult in many positions due to the small area of the wound, and the strength of the binding on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The swelling of the vein in the middle helps because it draws blood from above the head and below the body, for which it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to be careful for the nerve that is below, and if he punctures too deeply and finds the nerve, and it swells and the patient becomes seriously ill, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in some people due to its subtlety, then you must cut it with an anesthetic instrument; and protect the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The swelling of the cephalic vein helps because it draws blood from the head and assists the eyes; and it is necessary to puncture it with olive oil or myrtle oil, for it is the safest of all veins, as there is neither a nerve nor an artery below it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest vein, and it does not matter if one fails at first, and one retries; and by chance some veins swell when failing the first time, but it does not matter.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the sanie is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is performed not for any other reason but to preserve health and to avoid future illnesses; and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins found on the arm: namely, cephalic, basilic, and femoral; and one should undergo bloodletting at the beginning of spring, in autumn, and in winter after meals, when the sign of repletion appears; and one should undergo bloodletting on the first or third day, two or three hours into the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The medicine which is administered to the diseases has no fixed time, but when there is need of day or night, in all hours and at all times; and it does not befit to medicate children until fourteen years, nor a woman carrying child from the fourth month up to seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And those who have passed sixty years should not be medicated either.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to be medicated in any manner, it is necessary that they cleanse the intestines with a light enema if there is much retained bile so that the veins do not attract harmful superfluous substances from the intestines; nor should one who is overly satiated with food or drunk be medicated until they are sober, nor those suffering from dropsy; and beware of medicating after severe colic, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent intercourse with a woman, laborious work, sleeplessness, and fasting, which exhaust all strength, whether by weapon or body exertion; then refine the humors if the blood is thickened through food, drinks, and medicines, if you have the power to do so; then enter into a bath, unless something prevents it, to refine the blood, and be medicated from the vein of the arm around the third hour as we have said; and guard yourself that day from labor, pain, and lust, and similar things; and be cheerful and joyful, and let the medicator be higher than the one being medicated, and they should rub the arm two or three times, then moderately bind the ligature above it because when it is too tight or loose, blood cannot flow; and then rub the area with their hands until the veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the medicator’s flame with a little old oil, then place their left hand on that vein below where they wish to medicate so that the vein does not shrink when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee like strings to the surgeon, and there are such that are full of windiness, so when one applies fire upon them, they recoil from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these; and if he works the vein, then the wound becomes too narrow, for this reason it is necessary that the surgeons be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein works the first time, it is good; if not, then begin again a little below that place or above quickly, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the place is swollen and the patient is afraid, leave it for one or two days without loosening the arm: perhaps a warm abscess will come; do not enter into the bath, then resume the surgery if he wishes; and if the opening is small and the blood flows thinly and you fear that not enough blood will flow, then apply fire directly to that opening with all the flame; work quickly a little, although the place may be swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not begin the dressing again, and put on a poultice of oil lees, for it lightens the body of blood, and is more effective in this case the lees than the oil; and thus administer the oil lees in each dressing that you dress the veins to stop the flow of blood; and the same does treacle and bull's bile when they are put on the place; they refine the blood and it disperses when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, especially when it is not dressed before the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put on the place a sponge soaked in water and salt one pou chaut, and bind it for an hour; and you must do this after the flow of blood from the vein, and if there remains any blackness or greenness at the place after some days, it does not harm; and if you wish, put on something of aloes or murr mixed in juice of calamus, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and swelling appear at the suture of the basilical bone: therefore put your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft under the pressure of the hand, then that swelling is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore putting anything on what we have said, for fear that it might cut into the artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each the blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for him who is full and strong, and has need of bloodletting, that a larger wound be made, and let the flames be wide; and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and he must be cauterized little and often, and one should cauterize him by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of cauterization is safe from blood flow and nerve severing, and is better than long or wide cauterization.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him whose body is lacking in cauterization, it is necessary to give bread moistened in pomegranate juice; if he is heated, let blood three or four times. And if he is of a cold temperament, let him eat before cauterization bread moistened in musk syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints at the incision, after the release of much blood, then it is necessary that he inhales broth of meat, and subtle fragrant syrup, and uses other things we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bleed one arm and incise another at times, then it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds a little by little, according to the amount of his continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if one wants to bleed one arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, then he should bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wishes to be bled from another side, one must be bled on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that is already heated and brings on fever; one must draw off great quantities and widen the opening until it flows freely. When you restore all the conditions for bleeding, place your hand over their pulse while they are being bled, so death does not come instead of free flow, which often happens when the bleeder is negligent; and it should not be done when you wish to release the arm and allow blood to flow a second time, if the opening is closed, that you press forcefully on it. Nor should it be done if it is bent, that they extend their arm hastily, for this would be harmful; but leave it until it bleeds freely a second time; or you prick with the tip of the blade until the blood which is frozen at the vein’s opening flows out, and place over it a pouch filled with warm water, and press lightly on it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, then leave it alone and do not constrict it until the abscess has calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is need to bleed for the second time, then bleed in the same place or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein inside the arm is bled instead of the vein of the head because it is composed that way.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of bleeding is that the patient puts their hand in warm water until the fingers are red; then it should be tied moderately so that the vein appears well, then bleed now across, not wide nor long; and let the incision be large, and bleed close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, put the hand back in warm water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, for it is used more in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins because there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The swelling of the palm of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the method: draw out the hand, and put it in hot water until the veins are swollen so that they can be seen; if you cut across it, and if you cut it completely through, it does not matter; do not go too deep, because the nerves are all exposed under the flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as is necessary, put oil and tar on the veins to quickly seal them, and do this for each incision.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The swelling of the palm on the left hand is good for the disease of the spleen, and do it all as I have said for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of sophene is worth for all the diseases that are below the body, like diseases of the marrow, and retention of urine, and disease of the kidneys, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its salve is that the patient puts their foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it peres [Note: 'perer' could mean to wear away or disappear], and applies it over the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there are many veins; apply it then where the vein is widest, or at the ankle, which moves best.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you apply it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are below, and apply the salve across as well as when cutting; and let the flames be small.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the pus cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and let the vein fully drain.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the first attempt at bleeding fails, then begin again a little higher up, for the blood is salty; do not worry about the nerve, as we have said, and thus do the same with the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic is at the ankle of the foot, and its bleeding relieves the pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its bleeding is that the patient enters the bath and constrains above the ankle four times by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then bleed it in all ways you can, even crosswise; and it is better that you cut it, for the blood is salty, and it is very responsive to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then cut a vein from the back of the foot towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; and let so much blood as you wish, and then untie the bandage, and put on cotton and bind tightly; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of cupping treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping is made from horns, or of clay, or of glass; and cupping treatment is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping treatment without striking is done in two ways: either with full fire or without fire; and the cupping that involves striking and extracting blood is performed in fourteen areas of the body, one being at the very top of the head; another is in the neck; and two others on both sides of the neck; a cupping under the chin; cupping on both shoulders; cupping on the buttocks; cupping within both arms; cupping on both legs; cupping on both ankles; and this cupping does not draw blood, but rather from small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and for that reason it does not weaken a person as much as vein bleeding; and it should not be administered with full fire or without fire in any disease caused by excess, until all of the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of diseases it is required to bleed, or for customs, then we perform it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at any time; for there are such who, when they need to be bled, have heavy head; and there are such who find fullness and redness on their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and darkness before their eyes; and such who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and spit blood; and there are such who dream, and see by night blood and wounded and dead and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order it to be bled after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The salve of the ear thus helps with the dryness of the head … which comes to the eyes, and it is not right that this should be after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in the place of the cephalic salve, and it is not right for those who are of cold temperament to use it, or who have catarrh, because it does them much harm; and for this reason the elderly should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often recover from it become forgetful, and for this reason the cupping should be placed a little lower due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation on the neck is in place of the head salve and the basilic salve, and for this reason it is good for constriction of the breast, and to split the channel of the nostril, and for all, and for fullness; and there it should be applied lightly, because if it holds too firmly, it causes forgetfulness in the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Windings at the second ribs of the neck are good for headaches, ophthalmia and migraines, and for strangulation, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of basilica's application; and you must instruct the surgeon to press his hand when applying, that he not cut the artery, and there be no flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Windings below the chin are good for mouth diseases, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of applications to the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Windings on the shoulders are good for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Windings on the ribs are as good as those of the three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and instruct the surgeon not to press too much with a point, for the area is bare of flesh, and lies close to nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the anus, and for diseases below, and it must be large, and made of horn so it can draw well; and by chance, if it were delicate, it would break; and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs purge openly, for they draw blood from throughout the body, and are good for old pains in the reins, and of the bladder, and renew the flowers; and they are used instead of two sophenes, and of the two ankles, and always they weaken the body after long use, and cause faintness in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the suction cup is to first place it empty, and suck moderately, and apply it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not stop until you see the area red and swollen, and appear the redness of blood; then stop, and reapply the suction cups, and be mindful of the condition of the body, for there are those who have too much flesh, and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike only once, and make wide cuts, and a bit deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, then it must be struck twice: the first time to refine the course of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, then it must be struck a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we strike only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, then we repeat often; and if the vein is thick, then strike fully, and the end result is that the flow should be pierced suddenly, and it must be for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the sites of the cupping with opening and dissolving oil: if it is in winter, of violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil; and if it is in summer, of watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, then take oil of marjoram, or of balm, or oil of aniseed, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one who is being treated has tender flesh and large pores, then no oil should be applied, but it is necessary to wash after ventilation with rose water, or cold water, or water of black bindweed, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who have much moisture, it is lifted with ashes, or water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And for those who have thick excesses, they are lifted with old wine, or water of juice, or decoction of aniseed or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not right to treat with cupping before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two; and do not sleep after the cupping, and it is necessary that they exercise when they are about to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if the one who is healing is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed; then it is necessary that they take cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, lettuces with oil, and similar things; and eat porridge, and castrated animal meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And the one who has a cold constitution should take honey syrup, and moderate wine that is between old and new, and eat porridge, and eat porridge and small birds and pigeons; and on the day they will be bled, they must drink more than they eat; and it is necessary to give some people sometimes theriac or musk before or after bleeding to strengthen the main limbs; and the blood should be subtle, but those who are hot should not drink it.
