And in the one where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four types of dislocations, you should hurry to return the joint, extend it inward and outward, and move it left and right; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare one assistant strongly, and extend the leg forcefully with two hands, or with a rope tied above the knee; and another assistant extends his hand in such a way that he places his hands under the bones, then tightly binds a strong rope on the thigh; and another holds the end of the rope; and they extend upwards and downwards all at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at once and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to the four types, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then one must attend to its type. When the dislocation is outward, you should have the patient lie on his healthy side, then place the band at the root of the thigh and the spot below the angle, then extend the band upward toward the angle and toward the force; then take another assistant's arms, grasp the thick part of the diseased thigh, and stretch it upward forcefully: thus it will return to its place now; and this type of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot secure it in the manner we have said, then you must bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong band above the two heels and above the two knees, and let the diseased leg be stretched out twice as long as the other; then let him be hung from the top of a pole, and let him be raised up two arms' length off the ground; then command one assistant to grasp the head of the thigh, and have another assistant hanging with the patient who grasps the thigh forcefully, for the joint returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is in the thigh, the patient lies down, as we have said in that which has gilbositeit, and holds tightly the limb on the sick leg properly, and on the foot also; then places II sticks, I at the head and I other at the feet, then inserts I stick between the thighs of the patient inside the form; and has planted with moist cloths around, so it does not hurt the patient, then stretches each minister towards him, and the physician puts equally in his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put it on the table, and press it as we have said in the gilbositeit, and lay the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the diseased leg quickly, as I have said; and let the doctor place his hand on the diseased angle, then press with the other hand, and stretch downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is behind, it is not necessary to extend the patient downward or lift them up from the ground, but they should be positioned as if the hip were dislocated behind, just as we have said about lying on both hips; and let them lie on their face, and the limb should be extended as we have said before, and one must press on the joint with a table; and it will be correct when the patient extends his legs, and they will be equal; then align the thighs, apply the poultice, and strap it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let them rest for three or four days, then unbind them, and apply the poultice again; and if you see that they are equal, strap them as before, and leave them for three days; then unbind them, and make him walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: to be known, inward and outward, and backward; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign thereof is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it does not join with the thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your hands, then bend both sides of the knee firmly; and another minister extends his foot until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it joins well with the thigh lightly; and apply a plaster over it, and make the leg join with the thigh, and bind them together tightly for three or four days, then release the binding; and let not the patient work at walking until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not fully healed, apply strong extension as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is mended.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes displaced, and sometimes completely dislocated, inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and protrudes forward at the part where it is dislocated: the realignment is light, and one should gently extend it by hand when it is only displaced.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is entirely dislocated, then you must make the patient sit upright, and one minister holds firmly by the leg, above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left twice, then extend it upwards, and gently push the foot upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, then repeat the work, for it will return; and if it cannot be returned thus, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and place one stake firmly in the ground between his thighs, and wrap cloths around it so that it does not hurt the patient; then have the ministers hold the thigh, and another minister extends the foot with both hands or with a rope which is tied above the ankle; then each minister extends equally, and the stake should be between the patient's thighs to hold the patient in place when he is extended; then the doctor places the dislocation evenly with his hands, and another minister holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at the right point, put the plaster and bandages on, bind it properly, tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the heel behind, so the binding is not too tight; then leave it for two days or three, and if the binding softens, tighten it again; then untie it on the third day or fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if he walks before this time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses come, you must soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both are dislocated, they must be gently extended without effort, and this is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the foot's back, then you must make the patient sit on a flat place or on a table straight up, and put your foot on what appears of these joints, then press with your foot firmly until it returns; and when it is aligned, and nothing appears, then place under the sole of the foot a board at two points, then stretch it firmly, and leave it for three days, then release it; and make it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with the dislocation and you want to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the treatment if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for long, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and cautious, not bold; and use at the beginning things soothing hot abscesses, and leave the patient in God’s hands if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset now the limb to its place, even as the hot abscess comes; and when the limb is in place, then administer things soothing hot abscesses, and treat the wound with desiccating ointments as it should be; and if there is a fracture with the dislocation and small bones are detached, remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering into a path of fear according to what I have said, for this does not serve you well according to your Creator, and for the wisdom of your art and body.
Amen	Amen
